If the husband did not have intercourse, but if he had intercourse once and then became impotent, the woman will not have the option to annul the marriage. As stated in Durr Mukhtar: ... The third condition for annulment of the wife's marriage due to impotence is that from the time the wife learned of her husband's impotence, she did not expressly state her consent, e.g., she did not say, 'As he is, I will stay with him' – whether in private or in front of others. This is indicated by the absolute nature of the following narration, whether before or after deferment. As stated in Bada'i: 'The text explicitly states that dropping the option or its equivalent, whether after the qadi's giving of choice or before...' Also actions like cohabitation do not constitute consent. As stated in Khaniyah: ... Remaining conditions include that she be adult, not a [؟], and that she request separation, or her guardian if she is insane. If she has no guardian, the qadi appoints a man to litigate for her. As stated in Mula? and others. We leave these conditions for brevity. Indeed, some said that when a woman chooses herself after the qadi's giving of choice at the end, she becomes separated and does not need after that an annulment or divorce. In al-Mukhtar it is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Imam al-A'zam, she needs a qadi's ruling after her own choice. I said: The Imam's saying is the relied-upon in the reliable books and the most correct in narrations. And Allah knows best. ... She will stay because if she had clarified her consent, then she no longer has the right to demand separation. On this occasion, the wife's silence is not considered as her consent. As stated in Durr Mukhtar: ... The fourth condition for the one-year treatment of impotence is that when the qadi gives the wife the option after one year, she must choose separation in that same sitting. So if in that sitting she consented to her husband, or she remained silent until the sitting broke up – whether by her leaving or the qadi standing up – then her option becomes void, and separation cannot occur in any way. In Alamgiri: If she chooses her husband, or stands up from the sitting, or the qadi's assistants make her stand, or the qadi stands before she chooses, her option is void. As in al-Muhit. ... Also, besides the breaking of the sitting and the woman's leaving, there are other situations by which the sitting changes and the option becomes void.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of Hanafi rulings (rasm al-mufti) regarding the annulment of marriage due to impotence (inanah). The author extracts from authoritative sources like Durr Mukhtar, Bada'i, Khaniyah, and Alamgiri. The first ruling: if the husband has had intercourse even once before becoming impotent, the wife loses her right to seek annulment because her right was fulfilled by that intercourse. The second ruling: the wife must not have expressed consent to remain with the husband after learning of his condition; explicit verbal consent eliminates her right, but silence is not consent. The third ruling: the wife must be adult and not suffering from conditions like rutaq (vaginal occlusion) or qaran (bone growth) that would prevent intercourse. If she is insane, her guardian may seek annulment. The fourth ruling: after a one-year waiting period, the qadi gives her an option (khiyar) in a sitting; she must exercise it in that same sitting. If she leaves, or the qadi stands, the option is lost and cannot be revived. There is a known ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, even after the wife chooses annulment, she still needs a qadi's verdict (qada) to finalize the separation, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that her choice alone suffices. The author notes that the preferred position is Abu Hanifa's, as recorded in the soundest narrations. The passage also notes that other factors, such as the wife standing up or the qadi's assistants moving her, invalidate the option. This compilation serves as a practical guide for muftis issuing fatwas on impotence-related marriage annulments.

Key Terms
عنین (inan): A husband who is impotent and unable to have intercourse.
خیار (khiyar): The option given to the wife by the qadi after the one-year waiting period to either remain or seek annulment.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation or annulment of the marriage contract due to impotence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is required after the wife chooses annulment for impotence in the sitting?
A) She immediately becomes separated.
B) She must obtain a qadi's ruling to finalize the separation.
C) She must return the mahr.
D) She must wait another year.

Key Takeaway
A wife's right to annulment for impotence is tightly conditioned: no prior intercourse, no consent, timely exercise of khiyar in the same sitting, and according to the relied-upon view, a qadi's ruling is final.

Conditions and Procedure of Khiyar for the Impotent Husband's Wife
Explains the rules of khiyar for a woman married to an impotent man.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a wife to exercise the option due to her husband's impotence and identify which actions void the option.

Core Idea
The wife's option to separate due to impotence is lost if not exercised immediately in the same court sitting.

This passage from Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najiyah details the procedural requirements for a woman whose husband is impotent to seek separation. The text emphasizes that after a one-year waiting period, the judge gives her an option, but she must choose in that very sitting. Any delay or action indicating aversion, such as standing up or starting another conversation, nullifies her right. This lesson breaks down these conditions and their practical implications for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Act and Its Hukm
Determine that the wife is given an option (khiyar) after one year; the hukm is that it is a right that becomes void if not exercised in the same sitting.
The option is not a perpetual right; it is contingent on immediate action.
2
Extract the Conditions for Validity
From the passage, list: (1) one year of impotence, (2) qadi involvement, (3) exercise in the same majlis, (4) absence of aversion indicators.
The passage emphasizes these are not optional.
3
Analyze What Constitutes Aversion
The text states that any action indicating aversion (i'rad) voids the option, not just standing. Examples include starting a conversation or praying.
This is a key maxim: 'كل ما يدل على الإعراض يبطل الخيار'.
4
Note the Role of the Qadi
The qadi must be present; the woman cannot separate herself without a judge's decision.
This ensures order and proper assessment.
5
Determine Consequences
If she exercises option to stay or voids it, she loses right to future separation. If she chooses separation, mahr is still due and 'iddah required.
The passage ends with these consequences.

I will remain because if she has already clarified her consent, then she no longer has the right to demand separation, and in this situation, her silence will not be considered consent, as is in Durr al-Mukhtar. So if she had intercourse with a blind or impotent man, even if they argue for a long time, her right is not nullified. Al-Shami said: His statement 'and it is nullified' means [her right to] the mahr, and [if] she says 'I am pleased to stay with him' – such a condition. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit, volume 21. After one year of treatment for Hunayn, the fourth condition for his wife is that when after the expiry of one year the judge gives the wife the option, she must choose separation in that same sitting. So if in that sitting she chooses her husband, or she remains silent to the extent that the sitting disperses, whether by her leaving or by the judge standing up, then her option is void; separation cannot occur in any way. In al-Alamgiriyya: 'If she chooses her husband, or stands up from her sitting, or the judge's assistants make her stand up, or the judge stands up before she chooses, her option is void.' Thus in al-Muhit. The translation of the phrase: 'In the judge's name-giver [؟] it is that if a woman's husband gave her the authority to divorce herself, or the woman stood up from the sitting, or the judge's assistants made her stand up, or the judge stood up before she exercised her option, then her option is void.' Also, besides the sitting dispersing and the woman leaving, there are other forms that change the sitting and void the option, e.g., the woman starts another conversation, or begins to pray, etc., which indicate aversion or disregard. And the details of changing the sitting can be known from Sharh al-Shami, chapter Tafwid al-Talaq. The evidence that the nullification of the option is not confined to her standing or the judge standing, but rather everything that indicates aversion nullifies the option, is the statement of al-Durr: 'He said: The indication from both sides is evidence of aversion, whether she stands or [something else].' This indicates that 'standing' was mentioned as an example, and the intent is absolute aversion. This is what we have, and Allah knows best. Giving the impotent (namard) a respite of one year, and after completion of the year giving the wife the option, and if the husband refuses divorce then separating them – all these matters mentioned above require the judge's decision. Without a judge, the woman cannot separate herself. As in Radd al-Mukhtar under the statement of al-Durr: 'There is no consideration for the deferment of someone other than the judge of the town, because this is a prerequisite; the matter is only before the judge, which is the separation, so likewise the prerequisite.' And the general commentary of al-Shami, volume 2. And in a place where there is no judge, its detailed ruling has already passed in another section. The ruling on the seclusion of the impotent: Due to valid seclusion, the entire mahr becomes obligatory on the husband, and it is necessary to pay it even after separation. And it is also obligatory for the woman to observe the waiting period, as Sayyid al-Shami [wrote] in al-Durr.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal rulings related to the khiyar (option) granted to a woman whose husband is 'aneen (impotent). The text begins by clarifying that if a woman has expressly indicated her consent to stay with her impotent husband, she loses her right to demand separation later. Her silence in this context is not construed as consent. The passage then cites a ruling from Durr al-Mukhtar that even if the wife has intercourse with a blind or impotent husband, her right to claim separation is not nullified by the mere passage of time or arguments. The author then details the fourth condition for the exercise of the khiyar: after one year has elapsed, the qadi gives the woman the option, but she must exercise it in the same sitting. If she chooses her husband, remains silent until the sitting ends, or if she or the qadi leaves the sitting before she chooses, her option is void. The text expands on what constitutes a change of sitting: not only standing up, but any action indicating aversion, such as starting a new conversation or praying. Evidence is provided from the commentary of al-Durr that anything indicating aversion nullifies the option, using standing as an example. The passage then emphasizes that all these procedures require the involvement of a qadi; the woman cannot act on her own. Finally, it notes that valid seclusion with the impotent husband has already made the full mahr obligatory, which remains due even after separation, and the wife must observe the 'iddah.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): The option given to a wife to choose between staying with her husband or seeking separation due to his impotence after a one-year period.
عنِّين ('aneen): A man who is impotent and unable to have intercourse with his wife.
مجلس (majlis): The sitting in which the qadi gives the option and the woman must exercise it immediately; changing the majlis voids the option.
إعراض (i'rad): Aversion or turning away, indicated by actions like standing up, starting another conversation, or praying, which void the option.

Key Takeaway
The option of the wife of an impotent husband is a conditional right that requires immediate exercise in the presence of a judge; any indication of aversion nullifies it.

6 min
The Legal Maxim: Everything Indicating Aversion Voids the Option
Identifies the legal maxim governing the nullification of khiyar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal maxim 'كل ما يدل على الإعراض يبطل الخيار', list its furuat, and identify its istithna.

Core Idea
Anything indicating aversion voids the option – a Hanafi rule that extends beyond standing up.

This lesson extracts the underlying legal maxim from the passage on the impotent husband's wife. The text cites from al-Durr that the nullification of the option is not limited to standing up but includes any action indicating aversion. We explore the maxim's furuat and its exception, providing tools for applying this qawida in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim in Arabic and English
Write the maxim: كل ما يدل على الإعراض يبطل الخيار. It means: Everything that indicates aversion voids the option.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim, specific to khiyar cases.
2
Identify the Evidence from the Passage
The text directly quotes al-Durr: 'والدليل على أن بطلان الخيار لا يختص بقيامها وقيام القاضي بل كل ما يدل على الاعراض، بيطل الخيار'.
The evidence is a statement from a leading Hanafi text.
3
List the Furuat (Applications)
From the passage, extract the specific actions that void the option: standing up (by woman or judge), being made to stand, starting a conversation, praying, etc.
These are examples, not an exhaustive list.
4
Identify the Istithna (Exception)
The passage indicates that if the woman expressly chooses to stay with her husband, the option is not voided; she has exercised it.
This exception is based on the maxim 'الأمور بمقاصدها'.
5
Explain the Relationship to Other Qawaid
The maxim is related to 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' (Certainty is not removed by doubt) as a parallel, but they do not conflict.
The option is lost by clear aversion, not by mere doubt.

I will remain because if she has already clarified her consent, then she no longer has the right to demand separation, and in this situation, her silence will not be considered consent, as is in Durr al-Mukhtar. So if she had intercourse with a blind or impotent man, even if they argue for a long time, her right is not nullified. Al-Shami said: His statement 'and it is nullified' means [her right to] the mahr, and [if] she says 'I am pleased to stay with him' – such a condition. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit, volume 21. After one year of treatment for Hunayn, the fourth condition for his wife is that when after the expiry of one year the judge gives the wife the option, she must choose separation in that same sitting. So if in that sitting she chooses her husband, or she remains silent to the extent that the sitting disperses, whether by her leaving or by the judge standing up, then her option is void; separation cannot occur in any way. Also, besides the sitting dispersing and the woman leaving, there are other forms that change the sitting and void the option, e.g., the woman starts another conversation, or begins to pray, etc., which indicate aversion or disregard. And the details of changing the sitting can be known from Sharh al-Shami, chapter Tafwid al-Talaq. The evidence that the nullification of the option is not confined to her standing or the judge standing, but rather everything that indicates aversion nullifies the option, is the statement of al-Durr: 'He said: The indication from both sides is evidence of aversion, whether she stands or [something else].' This indicates that 'standing' was mentioned as an example, and the intent is absolute aversion. This is what we have, and Allah knows best. And it is also obligatory for the woman to observe the waiting period, as Sayyid al-Shami [wrote] in al-Durr.

Rulings for the Impotent Man ('Anin)
Detailing the rulings for the impotent man ('anin)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the 'anin to determine the wife's right to annulment, the requirement of qadi involvement, and the financial consequences based on the presence or absence of valid seclusion.

Core Idea
Only a qadi can annul an 'anin's marriage after one year; valid seclusion triggers full mahr and iddah.

This passage from Asraf Ali Thanwi's al-Hilat al-Najijah addresses the legal category of the 'anin (impotent man) and the detailed rules governing his marriage. It clarifies the wife's remedy, the role of the qadi, and the impact of valid seclusion on mahr and iddah. Understanding these distinctions is essential for issuing correct fatwas in family law disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and defect
The case involves an 'anin husband (impotent with intact organ) and his wife. The defect is inability to perform sexual intercourse.
The 'anin is distinct from khasi (castrated) and majbub (penis cut off).
2
Note the legal procedure
The wife must wait one year, then seek annulment only through the qadi. She cannot annul herself.
The qadi's decision is mandatory; without qadi, no annulment.
3
Determine mahr and iddah based on khalwah
Check if valid seclusion (khalwah sahiha) occurred. If yes, full mahr and iddah. If no, half mahr (or mut'ah) and no iddah.
Khalwah sahiha is equivalent to actual intercourse for these purposes.
4
Distinguish from other conditions
The khasi (missing testicles but organ intact) has the same ruling as 'anin. The majbub (penis cut off) has different rules not detailed here.
Proper classification of the husband's condition is critical for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنین (نامرد) کو ایک سال کی مہلت دینا اور ایک نامرد کی ندرست علاج سال پر سال پورا ہونے پر عورت کو اختیار دینا اور اُس کے بعد اگر شوہر طلاق سے انکار کرے تو تفریق کر دینا وغیرہ یہ تمام امور جو کہ اوپر مذکورہ ہیں قاضی کے فیصلے کے متحاج ہیں۔ قاضی کے بغیر عورت از خود تفریق نہیں کر سکتی۔ جیسا کہ ردالمختار قول الدر کے تحت ہے۔ ولا عبرة بتاجيل، غير قاضي البلدة لان هدا مقدمة امر لا يكون الاعند القاضى وهو الفرقة فكذا مقدمة والو الجنيه شامي شه ٢- اور جس جگہ قاضی موجود نہ ہو تو اس کا حکم تفصیلی طور پر دوسرے جزو میں گذر چکا ہے . عنائین کی خلوت کا حکم خلوت صحیحہ کی وجہ سے شوہر فین پر پورا مہر واجب ہو چکا تھاوہ تفریق کے بعد بھی ادا کرنا لازم ہے اور عورت پر عدت کرنا بھی واجب ہے جیسا کہ حضرت علامہ شامی نے در کے قول کے تحت تصویر فرمایا ہے : والا بانت بالتفريق من القاضي ولها كمال المحر وعليها العودة الوجود الخلوة الصحيحة بحر الرائق من جب یعنی ایسی عورت کا پورا مہر واجب ہے اور خلوت صحیحہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اُس پر عدت بھی ضروری ہے ۔ اور عالمگیری میں ہے : ولها المحمر كاملاً وعليهها العدة بالاجماع ان كان الزوج خلا بها. وان الويخل فلا عدة عليها و لها نظف المهران كان جسم والمتعة ان لم يكن مسمى كذا في البدائع اور مل ج ۲ - نامرد کی بیوی کا ہر اور عدت عبارت بالا کا ترجہ یہ ہے کہ ایسی عود - کا پورا مہر اور بالاجماع اس پر عدت ہے بشر طیکہ شوہر نے اُس عورت سے خلوت کی ہو اور اگر شوہر نے اُس سے . خلوت نہیں کی تو اس پر عدت نہیں ہے اور اس کا آدھا مہر ہے اگر مہر مقررہ ہے اور متاع ہے اگر مہر مقرر نہ ہو۔ الخ عضو مخصوص خصوص کئے ہوئے شخص کی بیوی کا حکم منین (نامرد کو ایک سال کی مہارت دینے کا حکم ہو او پر مذکور ہے صرف اس شخص کے لیے ہے جن کو کہ عرف میں عنین (ما مرد) کہتے ? ہیں اور بغیر خصیہ کا شخص یعنی جس کا عضو مخصوص ہو وہ بھی عین کے اکاری نہ ہوا ساتھ شامل ہے یعنی اس کا حکم بھی عنین جیسا ہے لیکن وہ شخص جس کا تعضم مخصوص کٹ گیا ہو خواہ تنہا یا خصیوں کے ساتھ کٹ گیا ہو جس کو فقہ کی اصطلاح میں محبوب یعنی عضو مخصوص کٹا ہوا کہتے ہیں۔ اور اسی طریقہ سے جس
Giving a year's respite to an impotent man ('anin), and when the year is completed, giving the woman an option, and thereafter if the husband refuses to divorce, the qadi annuls the marriage. All these matters mentioned above require the qadi's decision; without a qadi, the woman cannot annul herself. As in Radd al-Muhtar under the statement of al-Durr: 'There is no consideration for the respite given by someone other than the qadi of the town, because this is a preliminary to a matter that only occurs before the qadi, namely annulment, so too the preliminary.' [and al-Shami?] And where no qadi exists, its detailed ruling has passed in another section. The ruling of seclusion for the impotent: due to valid seclusion, the entire mahr became obligatory on the husband; he must pay it even after annulment, and the woman must observe iddah. As Allama Shami has described under the statement of al-Durr: 'And she becomes separated by annulment from the qadi, and she is entitled to the full mahr, and iddah is obligatory upon her due to valid seclusion.' (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) So such a woman is entitled to full mahr, and due to valid seclusion, iddah is also necessary. And in al-Alamgiriyya: 'She is entitled to the full mahr, and iddah is obligatory upon her by consensus if the husband had seclusion with her. If he did not have seclusion, then no iddah upon her, and she is entitled to half the mahr if the dower was specified, and to mut'ah if the dower was not specified.' (al-Bada'i) The summary of the above statements: such a woman is entitled to full mahr, and by consensus iddah is upon her, provided the husband had seclusion with her. If the husband did not have seclusion with her, then no iddah upon her, and she gets half the mahr if specified, and mut'ah if not specified. The ruling of the woman whose husband has a missing specific organ: The ruling of giving a year's respite to the impotent mentioned above applies only to the person whom custom calls 'anin (impotent). And a person whose testicles are missing but the organ is present is also included with the 'anin? Actually, his ruling is like that of the 'anin. But the person whose specific organ is cut off, whether alone or with the testicles, who is called 'majbub' (i.e., whose organ is cut off), and in this way...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling (hila) regarding the 'anin (impotent man). The Hanafi madhhab grants the wife of an 'anin the right to seek annulment (tafriq) after one year of patience, but this annulment must be executed by the qadi; she cannot do it herself. The text clarifies that if no qadi exists, the matter is handled differently and refers to another section. The author then discusses the financial consequences: if there was valid seclusion (khalwah sahiha), the full mahr is obligatory and must be paid even after annulment, and the wife must observe iddah. If there was no seclusion, she gets half the mahr (if specified) or a gift (mut'ah), and no iddah. The text cites Radd al-Muhtar, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya as sources. Finally, the passage distinguishes between different types of male incapacity: the 'anin (impotent with organ intact but unable to perform), the khasi (castrated, i.e., missing testicles but organ intact), and the majbub (one whose penis is cut off). The 'anin and khasi have the same ruling (one-year wait and annulment), while the majbub is treated differently. This is crucial for fatwa: the legal category depends on the specific physical condition.

Key Terms
عنین ('anin): A man who is impotent, unable to have sexual intercourse despite having an intact organ.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwah sahiha): Valid seclusion between husband and wife without physical or legal barriers to intercourse.
محبوب (majbub): A man whose specific organ (penis) is cut off, either alone or with the testicles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of the mahr for the wife of an 'anin if there was valid seclusion?
A) Half the mahr
B) Full mahr, must be paid after annulment
C) No mahr
D) Mut'ah only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on the 'anin requires qadi involvement for annulment; valid seclusion triggers full mahr and iddah, while its absence reduces mahr and eliminates iddah.

Mahr and Iddah after Judicial Separation: Condition of Khalwa Sahiha
Ruling on full mahr and iddah for woman separated by judge when valid seclusion occurred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mahr and iddah after judicial separation by identifying the condition of khalwa sahiha and determining whether full or half mahr and iddah apply.

Core Idea
Full mahr and iddah are wajib by consensus if valid seclusion occurred; otherwise half mahr and no iddah.

This passage establishes the Hanafi rule, grounded in scholarly consensus (ijma), that a woman separated by a judge (tafriq) receives the full mahr and must observe iddah only if valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) took place. The conditionality protects against uncertainty regarding pregnancy. Understanding this rule is essential for issuing correct fatwas in family law cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Recognize that the passage addresses judicial separation (tafriq), not divorce (talaq) or annulment (faskh).
The source text mentions 'al-tafriq min al-qadi'.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Note the condition of khalwa sahiha: if it occurred, full mahr and iddah; if not, half mahr and no iddah.
The text says 'in kana al-zawju khala biha' and 'in lam yakhlu'.
3
Analyze the proof
The ruling is supported by ijma (consensus) as stated in al-‘Alamgiriyya: 'bi al-ijma'.
Ijma is a definitive proof (qat'i) in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply to a case
Given a factual scenario, determine if khalwa sahiha was present, then state the mahr and iddah obligations.
Khalwa sahiha requires privacy, ability to consummate, and no impediment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كے قول کے تحت تصویر فرمایا ہے : والا بانت بالتفريق من القاضي ولها كمال المحر وعليها العودة الوجود الخلوة الصحيحة بحر الرائق من جب یعنی ایسی عورت کا پورا مہر واجب ہے اور خلوت صحیحہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اُس پر عدت بھی ضروری ہے ۔ اور عالمگیری میں ہے : ولها المحمر كاملاً وعليهها العدة بالاجماع ان كان الزوج خلا بها. وان الويخل فلا عدة عليها و لها نظف المهران كان جسم والمتعة ان لم يكن مسمى كذا في البدائع اور مل ج ۲ - نامرد کی بیوی کا ہر اور عدت عبارت بالا کا ترجہ یہ ہے کہ ایسی عود - کا پورا مہر اور بالاجماع اس پر عدت ہے بشر طیکہ شوہر نے اُس عورت سے خلوت کی ہو اور اگر شوہر نے اُس سے خلوت نہیں کی تو اس پر عدت نہیں ہے اور اس کا آدھا مہر ہے اگر مہر مقررہ ہے اور متاع ہے اگر مہر مقرر نہ ہو۔ الخ
He explained under his saying: 'And she is separated by the judge and she has the full mahr and upon her is the iddah due to the existence of valid seclusion' – from Bahr al-Raiq. Meaning: Such a woman has full mahr wajib and due to valid seclusion, iddah is also necessary upon her. And in al-‘Alamgiriyyah: 'And she has full mahr and upon her is the iddah by consensus if the husband secluded with her. And if he did not seclude, then no iddah upon her and she has half the mahr if it was specified, and a gift if not specified' – as in al-Bada’i. The summary of the above statement: Such a woman has full mahr and by consensus iddah is upon her, provided that the husband secluded with that woman. And if the husband did not seclude with her, then no iddah upon her, and she has half the mahr if it is specified, and a gift if it is not specified etc.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the mahr (dower) and iddah (waiting period) for a woman whose marriage is dissolved by a judge's decree of separation (tafriq). The source text is from al-Bahr al-Raiq and al-‘Alamgiriyya. The key condition is whether there was valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) between the spouses before the separation. If valid seclusion occurred, the woman is entitled to the full mahr and must observe iddah by consensus of the scholars. If no seclusion occurred, she does not observe iddah, and she receives either half the specified mahr or a gift (mut‘a) if no mahr was specified. This is consistent with the Hanafi position that iddah is to ascertain whether there is a pregnancy, and valid seclusion makes pregnancy possible. The ruling is cited as part of the rules governing 'innah (impotence) cases, as separation due to impotence falls under judicial separation.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwa sahiha): Valid seclusion between spouses where there is no physical or legal impediment to intercourse.
عدت (idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after termination of marriage before she can remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on mahr and iddah for a woman judicially separated from her husband after valid seclusion according to the Hanafi consensus?
A) Half mahr and no iddah
B) Full mahr and no iddah
C) Full mahr and iddah
D) Half mahr and iddah

Key Takeaway
Mahr and iddah after judicial separation depend on the occurrence of valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha); without it, the woman receives half mahr and no iddah.

Ruling for the Majbub and Those with Extremely Small Penis
Rule distinguishing immediate option for majbub from deferment for 'inin, with procedural aspect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ruling for a majbub, apply the qiyas to cases of extremely small penis, and outline the inspection procedure when the condition is disputed.

Core Idea
The majbub and those with extremely small penis are given immediate option; no one-year deferment.

In Hanafi marriage law, the wife of an impotent man ('inin) is given a one-year waiting period to see if he can be cured before she can seek annulment. However, this delay does not apply when the husband's penis is amputated (majbub) or so extremely small that intercourse is impossible. The judge must give the wife an immediate option to annul the marriage. This lesson explains the legal distinction, the underlying analogy, and the procedure for verifying the condition when disputed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key categories
Distinguish between 'inin (impotent with intact organ), majbub (amputated), and those with extremely small penis. The ruling for each differs.
The term 'majbub' includes amputation alone or with testicles.
2
Understand the default rule for the 'inin
The 'inin is given one year to attempt a cure. If still unable after a year, the wife may seek annulment. This is the baseline.
This one-year wait is a Hanafi-specific rule.
3
Recognize the exceptional rule for the majbub
The majbub's condition is incurable; therefore no wait is given. The wife has the immediate right to annulment.
Confirmed by Fatawa 'Alamgiriyya and Fatawa Qadi Khan.
4
Apply the qiyas to extremely small penis
The text states that the extremely small penis is 'annexed' to the majbub by analogy. The underlying cause ('illa) is the permanent impossibility of achieving penetrative intercourse.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
5
Outline the inspection procedure when disputed
If the wife claims the husband is majbub and he denies, the judge may appoint a trustworthy person to inspect and report. This ensures justice while preserving dignity.
The permissibility of inspection is derived from necessity and the principle of maslahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عضو مخصوص خصوص کئے ہوئے شخص کی بیوی کا حکم منین (نامرد کو ایک سال کی مہارت دینے کا حکم ہو او پر مذکور ہے صرف اس شخص کے لیے ہے جن کو کہ عرف میں عنین (ما مرد) کہتے ہیں اور بغیر خصیہ کا شخص یعنی جس کا عضو مخصوص ہو وہ بھی عین کے اکاری نہ ہوا ساتھ شامل ہے یعنی اس کا حکم بھی عنین جیسا ہے لیکن وہ شخص جس کا تعضم مخصوص کٹ گیا ہو خواہ تنہا یا خصیوں کے ساتھ کٹ گیا ہو جس کو فقہ کی اصطلاح میں محبوب یعنی عضو مخصوص کٹا ہوا کہتے ہیں۔ اور اسی طریقہ سے جس شخص کا عضومخصوص قدرتی طور پر بہت کم نہ ہونے کے مثل ہو اس کو ایک سال کی جہات دینے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ بلکہ پہلی ہی درخواست پر محبوب ( مقطوع الذکرم) وغیرہ ہونے کی تحقیق کر کے عورت کو اختیار دے دیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ فتاوی عالمگیری میں ہے : ولو وجدت المرآة زوجها مجبوباً خيرها القاضي لفعال وله يو رجل كذافي فتاوی قاضی خان - ويلحق بالمحبوب من كان ذكره صغير أجدًا الخرباب العنين ما ج ۲ - ترجمہ یعنی اگر کسی عورت نے شوہر کو مصنو مخصوص کٹا ہوا پایا تو قاضی عضو ایسی عورت کو فوری طور پر (فتح نکاح کا اختیار دے دے گا اور ایسے شخص کو ایک سال کی مہلت نہیں دی جائے گی۔ قاضی خان اور محبوب بینی عضو مخصوص کئے ہوئے میں وہ شخص بھی داخل ہے کہ جس کا عضو مخصوص بہت چھوٹا ہو۔ تتجه هذه الفائدة نامرد کی شرم گاہ کے معائنہ کی گنجائش اگر عورت دعوی کر سے کہ میرا شوہر عضو کٹا ہوا محبوب ہے اور مرد اس سے انکار کرے اور معائنہ کے بغیر اس بات کا فیصلہ نہ ہو سکے تو معائنہ بھی جائز ہے پس قاضی کسی معتبر شخص سے کہ دے کہ معائنہ (جانچ کر کے بتلاؤ کہ عورت سچ کہتی ہے یا مرد سچا ہے ۔ جیسا کہ قتادی شامی من ج 1 میں ہے "ولو الحبوب صغيرا المخ من جملہ عنین سے تفریق میں مالکیہ احناف میں مطابقت عین رنا مرد) اور اس میں من کی کی بیوی میں تفریق کا حکم
The ruling for the wife of a man whose private part is specifically [removed/small]... The ruling of giving a one-year deferment to the impotent man ('inin) is only for that person who in custom is called 'inin (impotent). And the person without testicles, i.e., whose private part exists, he is also included in the category of 'inin, meaning his ruling is like the 'inin. But the person whose private part is amputated, whether alone or with testicles, who in fiqh terminology is called majbub (one whose penis is amputated). And similarly, the person whose private part is naturally extremely small, like one that cannot function, there is no need to give a one-year deferment. Rather, on the first application, after verifying that he is majbub (maktu' al-dhakar) etc., the judge will give the woman the option. As in Fatawa 'Alamgiriyya: 'If the woman finds her husband to be a majbub, the judge gives her the option immediately...' And in Fatawa Qadi Khan: 'And annexed to the majbub is he whose penis is extremely small.' Translation: If a woman finds her husband's penis amputated, the judge will immediately give her the option to annul the marriage, and such a person will not be given a one-year deferment. Qadi Khan: And included in the majbub (penis amputated) is that person whose penis is very small. This benefit: The permissibility of inspecting the private part of the impotent man. If the woman claims that her husband is a majbub (amputated) and the man denies, and without inspection the matter cannot be decided, then inspection is permissible. So the judge should appoint a trustworthy person to inspect and report whether the woman is truthful or the man. As in Quduri? Shami: '...'
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage explains two important distinctions in Hanafi law regarding impotence and physical defects. First, the one-year deferment (imhal) is specific to the 'inin, i.e., a man who is naturally impotent due to lack of desire or ability to have an erection, but whose male organ is intact. This one-year wait is to see if he can be cured. However, a man who is majbub (has had his penis amputated) is not given this wait; his condition is incurable, so the wife is immediately given the option (khiyar) to seek annulment of the marriage. Similarly, a man whose penis is extremely small ('extremely' e.g., like a wart or non-functional) is also treated as majbub and given immediate option. Second, the passage addresses the procedure when the wife claims her husband is majbub and he denies. The judge may order a physical examination by a trustworthy person to verify the claim. This reflects the Hanafi principle of facilitating the woman's right to a marriage free from detrimental defects, while also protecting the husband's privacy through a dignified procedure.

Key Terms
عنین ('innin): A man who is impotent, unable to have intercourse due to lack of erection, but his organ is intact.
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis is amputated or missing.
مقطوع الذکر (maqtu' al-dhakar): Same as majbub: one whose penis is cut off.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following men is given a one-year deferment before the wife can seek annulment?
A) The majbub
B) The 'inin
C) The man with extremely small penis
D) The eunuch (majbub along with testicles)

Key Takeaway
The majbub and those with extremely small penis are given immediate annulment right, no one-year wait, because their condition is incurable.

Wife's Right to Annul Marriage Due to Husband's Insanity: Hanafi Ikhtilaf and Fatwa Hierarchy
Ruling on wife's option to annul due to husband's insanity with Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy to determine the operative ruling when a wife seeks annulment due to her husband's insanity, distinguishing between the positions of Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad, and state the conditions for each position.

Core Idea
The wife's right to annul for husband's insanity is disputed within the Hanafi school: Shaykhayn deny it, Imam Muhammad grants it under unbearable hardship.

This passage addresses a critical family law issue: can a wife annul her marriage if her husband becomes insane? Within the Hanafi school, there is significant ikhtilaf between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad. The passage also distinguishes between sudden and innate insanity, drawing analogies to impotence and eunuch cases. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for a mufti, as later fatwa collections prefer Imam Muhammad's view for relief. We will dissect the arguments, conditions, and the fatwa hierarchy to determine the operative ruling today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
First, note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) do not grant the wife an automatic right to annul due to insanity alone. Only if the insanity prevents consummation is it treated like impotence with a one-year wait. Imam Muhammad, however, gives the wife the option if the insanity is so severe that she cannot bear living with him, e.g., fear of being killed.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the Shaykhayn's view is the default in mu'amalat, but Imam Muhammad's view is adopted for hardship cases.
2
Distinguish between sudden (hadith) and innate (asli) insanity
The passage clarifies: if the insanity is sudden and curable, it is like impotence (inneen) — the wife must wait one year. If it is innate or incurable, it is like being a eunuch (jabb) — the wife has an immediate option to seek annulment without delay.
This distinction affects the waiting period and the immediacy of the wife's right.
3
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
Later Hanafi sources (e.g., Hadai Qudsi) adopt Imam Muhammad's view for fatwa, especially when the wife faces unbearable hardship. The Shaykhayn's view is considered stricter and may be set aside to prevent harm. Identify which view is mufta bihi and why.
The mufta bihi is Imam Muhammad's position in cases of severe hardship, as indicated in the passage.
4
Compare with other schools
The passage notes that Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanbali schools generally grant the wife the right to annul due to insanity and other serious defects. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence is that a Hanafi mufti may need to consider Imam Muhammad's view to align with other schools in modern contexts.
This comparison helps in inter-madhhab fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

للامام محمد (صفحه بس باب ما يذكرنى النكاح من الجنون محمد قال قال البوحنيفه في المجنون تخاف منه امرأنه ولو يجامعها انه افكان لا يفيق جدل بين امرائه وبين ما يخاف عليها منه في حال الخوف والفقة عليها من ماله ونو يفرق بينهما الا ان يخلى بينه وبينها ولا يصل اليها فاذا كان ذلك اجل سنة فان وصل اليها والأخيرت فان اختارت المقامر معاه انفق عليها من ماله ولم يكن لها بعد ذلك خيار وان اختارت الفرقة بانت بتطليفة انتهى منه عد ويؤيد ما في منحة الخالق على البحر الرائق حيث قال قوله فالمجنون كفوء للعاقلة رفيه اختلاف المشائخ قال في الخمر وقيل بختير لاندينيت مقاصد النكام فكان الشد من الفقر ودناة الحرقة وينيغي اعتماده لان الناس يعيرون بتزويج المجنون اكثر من وفي المعرفة وفي البناية من المرغيناني لا يكون كفر ألعاقلة الخ است ج ٣)
According to the saying of Muhammad, she has the option if he is in a state in which she cannot bear living with him. And in the book al-Athar of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), similarly if she finds him insane, paranoid, she fears that he may kill her. [Reference] page chapter 'A man marries and has a defect.' And in al-Fatawa al-Hamadiyya by Allama Rukn ibn Husam al-Naguri (page 72) from al-Mudmarat, Muhammad said: If the husband has a defect that prevents him from reaching his wife, then the woman has choice. Then it is looked at: if the defect is like sudden insanity, leprosy, and the like, then it is like impotence; he is waited for a year. And if the insanity is innate or a disease from which recovery is not hoped, then it is like being a eunuch; she has the option: if she wishes she stays with him, and if she wishes she raises the matter to the court so that separation is effected. From the mentioned statements it is understood that according to the two shaykhs, the woman does not have the right to annul the marriage due to the husband's insanity. But according to Imam Muhammad, she has this right: she can apply to the judge for separation and get herself freed from the marriage with the insane, provided the insanity is of such a degree that living with him is impossible, e.g., fear of being killed. (etc.) The discussion of insanity that gives right to annulment: the principle is that the insanity that gives the woman the right according to Imam Muhammad... that is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, if insanity occurs before consummation and during insanity he cannot have intercourse, then according to Abu Hanifa such an insane is in the ruling of an impotent man (inneen): a year's respite is given, and separation is effected in the same way... And near [Imam Muhammad] the right of annulment can be obtained. The reason for it is expressed in different words: in al-Mabsut the words are 'she cannot bear living with him', and in Kitab al-Athar it is mentioned 'fear that he may kill her'. Synthesis: that insane who causes unbearable hardship, the ruling is such. ... Regarding the wife of an insane, the opinion of the three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) is also that she has the right of annulment due to insanity etc. And in Shadi... it is reported that the saying of Imam Muhammad is to be adopted. And regarding the saying of [the other imams?], there is detail: if the insanity is sudden (hadith), then the judge gives a one-year period to the insane person and his guardians like an impotent man. As in the book al-Hajj of Imam Muhammad... It is supported by what is in Minhah al-Khaliq 'ala al-Bahr al-Ra'iq where he said: his saying 'the insane is compatible for the sane woman' has difference of the mashayikh. He said in al-Khum... and it is said that choice is for religiosity and purposes of marriage, so the difficulty is from poverty and low character, and it is appropriate to adopt it because people criticize marrying an insane more... And in al-Binaya from al-Marghinani: he is not compatible for the sane woman... end.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the wife's right (khiyar al-faskh) to annul her marriage due to the husband's insanity, along with the ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams. The text opens by citing Imam Muhammad's position: the wife has the option if the insanity is at a level where she cannot bear living with him, supported by Kitab al-Athar which adds fear of being killed. Then it quotes al-Fatawa al-Hamadiyya distinguishing between sudden insanity (treated like impotence with a one-year wait) and innate insanity (immediate option). The Urdu commentary explains that the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) do not grant this right, while Imam Muhammad does, provided the insanity causes unbearable hardship. It then clarifies the principle: if insanity occurs before consummation and prevents intercourse, Abu Hanifa treats it like impotence (inneen) with a waiting period; otherwise, the wife has no option according to him. Imam Muhammad's view, however, gives the option based on hardship. The passage harmonizes the phrasing from al-Mabsut ('cannot bear living') and Kitab al-Athar ('fear of killing') by noting that such fear typically accompanies unbearable suffering. It also notes that the other three schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) grant the option, and some Hanafi fatwa collections prefer Imam Muhammad's view for relief. The final part discusses the compatibility of an insane man with a sane woman, citing Minhah al-Khaliq, indicating that the issue of compatibility (kafa'a) is separate from the option due to defect.

Key Terms
خيار فسخ (khiyar al-faskh): the right to annul the marriage contract due to a defect in the spouse
شيخين (shaykhayn): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
مجنون (majnun): a person suffering from insanity (in this context, the husband)
جنون حادث (junun hadith): insanity that occurs after marriage (sudden)
جنون أصلي (junun asli): insanity present before marriage or innate

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for the wife to have the right to annul the marriage due to her husband's insanity according to Imam Muhammad?
A) The insanity must be present before marriage.
B) The insanity must be of a degree that she cannot bear living with him, such as fear of being killed.
C) The husband must also be impotent.
D) The wife must obtain the permission of her guardian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on wife's annulment for husband's insanity follows Imam Muhammad's view: the wife has the right to annul if the insanity causes unbearable hardship, with a distinction between sudden (one-year wait) and innate (immediate option).

Wife's Right to Faskh for Husband's Dangerous Insanity
Rasm rule: procedure for faskh due to husband's insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki-influenced Hanafi procedure for a wife to obtain faskh due to her husband's dangerous insanity, and identify the conditions that must be met.

Core Idea
Dangerous insanity gives the wife the right to annul, but only after a one-year waiting period and upon meeting conditions.

In this passage, the author addresses a delicate family law issue: when a husband becomes dangerously insane, what recourse does the wife have? The ruling offers a procedure that blends Hanafi principles with Maliki caution, especially given the difficulty in distinguishing types of insanity. We will walk through the conditions, waiting period, and the annulment process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The husband is dangerously insane; the wife seeks annulment. Understand that not all insanity qualifies — only dangerous/continuous insanity gives the right.
Dangerous means causing harm or fear of harm.
2
Distinguish types of insanity
The text notes that distinguishing between continuous (mutbiq) and intermittent (hadith/mutawassit) insanity is unclear, so caution is taken by adopting the Maliki view that treats both the same.
Hanafi school may differentiate, but here Maliki is followed for precaution.
3
Outline the procedure
The wife applies to the court (or Shari'ah committee), proves dangerous insanity, the judge investigates, grants a one-year respite for treatment, and if the husband remains insane after the year, the wife may demand faskh.
The judge annuls the marriage retroactively (faskh).
4
State the conditions for the wife's option
1. The wife must not have known of the insanity before marriage. 2. After learning of the marriage, she must not have expressed consent. Also, minor insanity does not give the right to annul.
These conditions prevent misuse of the option.

From this it is known that according to them, continuous insanity (junun mutbiq) is that in which there is no lucid interval. But in the mentioned book, the word 'hadith' (acquired) is not present, due to which the interpretation of continuous and acquired insanity in relation to each other cannot be known. In short, the interpretation of 'hadith' and 'mutbiq' could not be completely clear and determined.
For this reason, caution in this is that in the Maliki school, for the insane there is a period of treatment, regardless of this detail, a period of one year is given for treatment in every case, and after that a decision is made, especially when the decision is not in the court of a Shari'ah judge. Rather, if the decision of the Muslim community's Shari'ah committee is made according to the Maliki school, then the respite etc. should also be given according to their school. And the school of these honorable persons is that continuous insanity and intermittent insanity have the same ruling, i.e., in both cases a one-year respite is given, as mentioned in your Maliki Arabic which is published with this treatise, in fatwa no. 19 of Hazrat Allama Salih Tunai, teacher of Masjid Nabawi, Madinah Munawwarah, with reference to Tuhfa. And the text in al-Muntakhab of al-Baji from the Malikiyyah: 'And 'Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan narrated concerning the insane, whether he has lucid intervals or is continuous, if he causes her harm and she fears [harm from him?], then [the judge] gives him a period of one year and orders maintenance for her from his wealth...' Summary of the phrase from 'Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan regarding the annulment of marriage due to insanity: that the insane, whether his insanity is intermittent or not, if he causes harm to the woman and she fears harm from him, then the judge will give the insane a respite of one year and order that the woman's maintenance be paid from the insane's wealth. If during this time the insane recovers, then good; otherwise the woman has the option to annul the marriage. The second form of the ruling of dangerous insane regarding separation is that the wife of the insane applies to the judge's court (or Shari'ah committee) and proves that the husband is dangerously insane. Then the judge (or Shari'ah committee) investigates the matter. If it is proven correct, then he gives the insane a respite of one year for treatment. When the year is complete, if the wife applies again and the husband's insanity still persists, then the woman is given the option. If upon that the woman demands separation in that same session of option, then the judge effects separation, i.e., annuls the marriage, as mentioned in the previous answer from Fatawa Alamgiri. (And this separation by the judge completely nullifies the marriage, i.e., the marriage is considered void ab initio, as the word 'faskh' is found in al-Athar and al-Mabsut of Sarakhsi, and the word 'faskh' is found in Fath al-Qadir etc. And the conditions for the wife's option for annulment that were previously detailed, most of those conditions also apply to the wife of an insane person. Their summary is: 1. The woman should not have known of the husband's insanity before marriage. 2. After coming to know of the marriage, the woman should not have expressed consent. It should be clear that for minor insanity, the woman does not have the right to annul the marriage, as is found in al-Mabsut and al-Athar.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal ruling (rasm rule) concerning the wife's right to seek annulment of marriage when the husband suffers from dangerous insanity. It begins by clarifying the types of insanity: mutbiq (continuous, no lucid intervals) and hadith (acquired, but here the text notes the lack of clarity in definitions). To avoid confusion, it recommends adopting the Maliki position out of caution, especially when the decision is not made by a formal Shari'ah court but by a Muslim community committee. According to the Maliki school, both continuous and intermittent insanity are treated the same: a one-year waiting period for treatment is given. The text quotes from Maliki sources, specifically 'Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan's narration, stating that if the insane husband causes harm or the wife fears harm, the judge grants a one-year respite and orders maintenance from the husband's wealth. If he recovers, the marriage continues; otherwise, the wife has the right to faskh. The passage then outlines the procedure: the wife applies to the court, proves the dangerous insanity, the judge investigates, gives one year for treatment, and if still insane after a year, the wife may demand separation, and the judge annuls the marriage. It notes that this annulment renders the marriage void ab initio (like it never existed). Finally, it lists two conditions for the wife's option: she must not have known of the insanity before marriage, and after learning of it, she must not have explicitly consented to the marriage. Importantly, minor insanity does not give the wife the right to annul. This ruling is based on Hanafi sources (Fatawa Alamgiri, al-Mabsut, al-Athar, Fath al-Qadir) but also references Maliki jurisprudence for precautionary adoption.

Key Terms
جنون مطبق (junun mutbiq): Continuous insanity with no lucid intervals.
فسخ (faskh): Judicial annulment of marriage, rendering it void ab initio.
مہلت (یک سال) (muhlat (yeh saal)): One-year respite for treatment granted by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Follow the Hanafi view strictly, allowing faskh only for continuous.
B) Adopt the Maliki view as a precaution, treating both types with a one-year waiting period.
C) Give no waiting period and annul immediately.
D) Wait for the husband to recover naturally without intervention.

Key Takeaway
Dangerous insanity in a husband gives the wife the right to annul the marriage after a one-year waiting period and subject to conditions of ignorance and non-consent; minor insanity does not qualify.

Loss of Wife's Right to Annulment Due to Consent After Husband's Madness
Explains conditions for loss of khiyar al-faskh for post-marriage junun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Maliki-derived rule on forfeiture of khiyar al-faskh when a wife consents after learning of her husband's madness, and distinguish between voluntary and forced intimacy.

Core Idea
A wife loses her khiyar only if she voluntarily permits intimacy after knowledge; coercion preserves her option.

This passage addresses a critical family law scenario: a wife whose husband develops madness after marriage. While the Hanafi school generally restricts annulment (khiyar al-faskh) to defects present at the time of contract, the Maliki school grants the option even for post-marriage madness. The author of this text, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, presents the Maliki view as a practical concession (hila) for the severe hardship of living with a mad husband, and details the precise conditions under which the wife forfeits her right—namely, voluntary consent after knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
Recognize that the passage concerns the wife's right to annul the marriage (khiyar al-faskh) due to the husband's madness that develops after the marriage.
The Hanafi school has no explicit position from Imam Muhammad, so the author turns to the Maliki school.
2
State the Maliki Ruling
According to the Maliki school (and Shafi'is/Hanbalis), the wife retains the right to annul even if madness arises after the marriage, but she loses it if she consents after learning of the defect.
Consent can be verbal or practical (tamkin).
3
Identify the Conditions for Forfeiture
For the option to be lost, three conditions must be met: (1) the wife must have knowledge of the madness, (2) she must voluntarily allow intercourse or its precursors (kissing, touching), and (3) the act must be her choice, not coerced.
Forced intimacy does not forfeit the option.
4
Note the Exception for Coercion
The text explicitly states that if the mad husband forces intercourse, the wife's right remains intact. This is because the word 'makkantahu' (made it possible) implies voluntary permission.
The exception protects the wife from losing her right under duress.
5
Distinguish from Impotence Case
The passage contrasts the wife of a madman with the wife of an impotent man (mu'tarid). In the latter case, tamkin does not indicate consent because the defect is internal; for the madman, the defect is obvious, so tamkin after knowledge shows acceptance.
This distinction is key to understanding why the rule differs.

Source Text

بساقط نہ ہو گا چنا نچہ عبارت مذکورہ میں لفظ مکنتہ کا لفظ اس پر صراحتہ دلالت کرتا ہے۔ نیز جنون کے ساتھ موجب للفسخ کی قید سے یہ معلوم ہوا کہ اگر ابتدائی جنون کے زمانہ میں اس سے پہلے کہ جنون اس درجہ کو پہنچے کہ جس سے نکاح فسخ کرنے کا حق حاصل ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ گذر چکا ہے اور اس کی تفصیل مشروع جواب میں ہے۔ ہمبستری یا اس کے دوائی پاتے جائیں اور بعد میں جنون بڑھ کر مذکورہ له والفرق بين حكو المعترض والمجنون ان تمكين امرأة المعترض لا يدل على الرضابل انما هو لاختيار ماله فانه لا يمكن بدارن التمكين ودواعي الوطى ولا كذلك امرأة المعنون فات الجنون ظاهر فالتمكين ودواعي الوطى بعد العلم بالجنون يدل على الرضاء بالمقامر معه وهو مسقط الخيار والله اعلم
Regarding the occurrence of madness after marriage: there is no clear statement from Imam Muhammad, but the Maliki school clarifies that if madness occurs after marriage, the woman still has the right to separation (as in al-Mudawwana al-Kubra). However, in their view, the condition is that after learning of the madness that gives the right to annulment, the wife does not voluntarily give her husband the opportunity for intercourse or its precursors (like kissing or touching). For if she does that, it becomes practical consent, which nullifies her right, just as verbal consent would. As Imam Khalil stated in al-Mukhtasar: 'The option of annulment is established with the Malikis, Shafi'is, and Hanbalis in five situations; and summarily from them, if the husband has madness, leprosy, or vitiligo...' And we take from this the exception of madness due to its frequency and severe necessity, not leprosy and vitiligo, as women can endure living with those unlike madness... This condition of consent shows that if the madman forced intercourse on the wife, her right to option is not lost, as indicated by the word 'made it possible' (makkantahu). Also, the condition that the madness must be of the type giving right to annulment shows that if initial madness before reaching that degree allowed intimacy, and later the madness intensified, the ruling is as stated. The difference between the wife of an impotent man (mu'tarid) and the wife of a madman is that the latter's consent indicates acceptance of living with him, which nullifies the option. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the khiyar al-faskh (right to annul the marriage) for a wife whose husband develops madness after the marriage. The author first notes that Imam Muhammad has no explicit statement on this, but then presents the Maliki view as a reference. According to the Malikis, the wife retains the option even if madness occurs later, but she loses it if she, after knowing the condition, voluntarily allows intercourse or its precursors (kissing, touching). This is because such actions indicate consent to the marriage, which forfeits the right. The author draws a parallel: just as verbal consent cancels the option, so does practical consent. The passage then cites Imam Khalil's Mukhtasar, confirming that Malikis, Shafi'is, and Hanbalis grant the option for madness, leprosy, and vitiligo, but the author notes that the extreme hardship in madness justifies its exception. A crucial detail is added: if the mad husband forces intercourse, the wife's right remains intact—only voluntary permission nullifies it. Additionally, the madness must be of the degree that warrants annulment; early-stage madness that does not yet justify faskh does not trigger the same rule. The section concludes with a comparison with the case of an impotent husband (mu'tarid): his wife's consent does not indicate acceptance of the defect because his condition is internal, whereas a madman's insanity is apparent, so her consent after knowledge shows she accepts the condition, forfeiting her option.

Key Terms
خيار الفسخ (khiyar al-faskh): The wife's right to annul the marriage contract due to a defect in the husband, such as madness.
التمكين (al-tamkin): The wife voluntarily allowing her husband to have intercourse or engage in foreplay (kissing, touching) after knowing his defect.
دواعي الوطء (dawa'i al-wat'): Precursors to intercourse; actions like kissing and touching that lead to intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the rule presented in the passage, which of the following actions by the wife will NOT forfeit her right to annulment if she has knowledge of her husband's madness?
A) Voluntarily allowing intercourse after learning of the madness.
B) Voluntarily allowing kissing after learning of the madness.
C) The husband forces intercourse after she learns of the madness.
D) Verbally expressing consent to remain with him after learning of the madness.

Key Takeaway
A wife loses her right to annul the marriage for post-marriage madness only if she voluntarily permits intercourse or its precursors after knowing of the defect; coercion preserves her option.

Fatwa on the Missing Person's Wife: Hanafi Original and Maliki Dispensation
Explains Hanafi ruling on mafqud, contrasts Maliki view, and describes later Hanafi adoption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy to the case of a missing person's wife and construct a fatwa adopting the Maliki view based on necessity.

Core Idea
In Hanafi iftaa, necessity permits adopting the Maliki four-year rule for a missing person's wife.

The case of a missing person (mafqud) presents a dilemma: how long must a wife wait before remarrying? The Hanafi school is cautious, requiring a strong presumption of death. However, later Hanafi jurists, facing widespread social disruption, sometimes issued fatwas according to the Maliki school as a dispensation. This lesson explores the interplay between strict evidence and necessity in Hanafi iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default Hanafi position
State the original Hanafi ruling: the wife may remarry only after the judge rule on the husband's death based on strong presumption (ghalib al-zann) from circumstances like war or dangerous travel.
Strong presumption is a key concept; it is more than mere doubt.
2
Understand the criteria for ghalib al-zann
Identify what counts as strong presumption: disappearance at sea, war, banditry, or a dangerous road. The judge uses evidence, not conjecture.
Jami' al-Fatawa also includes loss in a Muslim kingdom if predominant.
3
Compare with the Maliki position
Imam Malik allows remarriage after four years from the judge's ruling, regardless of strong presumption, under certain conditions.
Imam Ahmad also agreed in some cases.
4
Recognize the shift: later Hanafi adoption
Later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirin) adopted the Maliki view in cases of necessity (darura) due to social fitna, as reported by Qahistani and Shami.
This is a fatwa dispensation, not a change in doctrine.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
Distinguish between the original Hanafi doctrine (from mutaqaddimin) and the operative fatwa under necessity (from muta'akhkhirin). The mufta bihi in times of widespread hardship may be the Maliki view.
See fatwa_hierarchy block below.

فقہ حنفی میں مفقود کی بیوی کے لیے حکم اس قسم کی صورتوں کے علاوہ فقہ حکم جنتی میں مفقود کی بیوی کے لیے اس کے علاوہ کوئی گنجائش نہیں ہے کہ مفقود کے ہم عر لوگوں کے ختم ہو نے پر قاضی اُس کے مرجانے کا فیصلہ کر دے اور اس کے بعد عورت عدت وفات گزار کر نکاح کرے۔ لیکن حضرت امام مالک رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے چند شرائط کے ساتھ کہ جن کی تفصیل عنقریب بیان ہوگی ہر ایک حالت میں ربیعنی مفقود کے ہلاک ہونے کا گمان ہو یا نہ ہو) مفقود کی بیوی کو حاکم کے فیصلہ کے بعد چار سال انتظار کر کے مدت گذر نے پر دوسرا نکاح کرنے کی اجازت دے دی ہے اور حضرت امام احمد نے بھی مفقود کی بعض صورتوں میں چار سال کی مدت کو اختیار فرمایا ہے ریعنی حضرت امام احمد نے بھی مفقود کی بیوی کو چار سال انتظار کر کے عدت وفات گزار کر نکاح ثانی کی اجازت دی ہے جیسا کہ معنی جلد و میں ہے۔
مسلم مفقود میں مالکیہ کے مذہب پر کل اریہ یہ ہے کہ مفقود الجر کے فسخ نکاح کے معاملہ میں حنفیہ کا مذہب دلائل کے اعتبار سے نہایت قومی اور غیر معمولی احتیاط پر مبنی ہے لیکن فقہاء حنفیہ رحیم اللہ میں سے بعض متاخرین نے نے وقت کی نزاکت اور فتنوں پر نظر فرماتے ہوئے اس مسئلہ میں حضرت امام مالک کے مذہب پر فیصلہ دے دیا ہے جیسا کہ حضرت علامہ شامی نے در منطقی اسے قہستانی کا جو کہ چوتھی صدی کے مشائخ حنفیہ میں ہیں قول نقل فرمایا ہے ۔ " دوافتی به موضع الضرورة
کے متقدمین علما اور متاخرین کی تعریف : تین صدی تک کے فقہاء کرام و متقدمین کہا جاتا ہے اور چوتھی صدی سے متاخرین کا اطلاق آیا ہے البنی جوشی صدی کے بعد کے علاء متاخرین کہلاتے جاتے ہیں جیسا کہ علامہ شامی کے مجمو در رسائل ابن عابدین میں سے رسالہ شفاء العلیل میں مذکور ہے
If he left home with a strong presumption of his death, or if he traveled by sea and no news of reaching the shore, then after waiting, the ruler will pronounce his death when the ruler has a strong presumption of his death. After knowing this, his wife may observe the waiting period of death and then marry. As in al-Shamiyya under the saying of al-Durr: 'al-Zayla'i chose to refer it to the imam.' He said in al-Fath: 'Whenever he sees the maslaha, he rules his death.' Its implication is that he exercises ijtihad and rules based on apparent signs indicating his death. On this is based what is in Jami' al-Fatawa: 'If he is lost in the kingdom (of Islam), it is predominant to rule his death, as if he is lost in a time of meeting the enemy or highway robbers, or he travels on a dangerous road, especially if his travel was by sea or the like, rule his death because it is predominant in these situations, even if there are two probabilities and the probability of death arises from evidence, not pure conjecture. This probability is like the probability when the missing person reaches an age beyond which one normally does not live, as they differed on its limit, quoted from al-Ghunya.' End of quote from Jami' al-Fatawa. Some of our eminent teachers adopted it and said that Qadizada, author of Bahr al-Fatawa, adopted it. But it is not hidden that it is necessary that a long period pass so that his death becomes predominant, not just loss without relying on meeting the enemy or sea travel and the like. (Vol. 3, p. 5). In Hanafi fiqh, besides such cases, there is no other latitude for the wife of the missing person. That is, when people of the missing person's contemporary generation die out, the judge decides his death and then the woman observes the waiting period of death and marries. But Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) with some conditions (whose details will soon be mentioned) in every case (whether there is a presumption of death or not) allowed the wife of the missing person, after the judge's decision, to wait four years and then, after the passage of the period, marry another. Imam Ahmad also in some cases of the missing person chose four years; i.e., Imam Ahmad also allowed the wife of the missing person to wait four years, observe the waiting period of death, and then marry another, as is in the meaning of volume such-and-such. In the missing person case, according to the Maliki school, the total opinion is that... Regarding the annulment of marriage of the missing person, the Hanafi school is based on very strong and extraordinary caution in terms of evidence, but some later scholars of the Hanafi school (may Allah have mercy on them), looking at the delicacy of the time and tribulations, have given a ruling in this issue according to the school of Imam Malik, as Allama Shami has quoted in Durr al-Muntaqa from Qahistani, who is among the fourth-century Hanafi scholars, saying: 'We issue fatwa with it (the Maliki view) in the place of necessity.' Definition of early and later scholars: Jurists up to the third century are called early (mutaqaddimin), and from the fourth century the term later (muta'akhkhirin) is applied. Actually, after the fourth century, scholars are called later, as mentioned in the treatise Shifa' al-'Alil from the collection of treatises of Ibn 'Abidin.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a legal discussion on the ruling concerning the wife of a missing person (mafqud) in Hanafi fiqh, with a comparison to the Maliki school, and a note on later Hanafi practice. The passage begins by describing the Hanafi position: a wife may remarry only after the judge (hakim) has ruled on the death of the missing husband based on a strong presumption (ghalib al-zann) of his death. Such presumption arises from circumstances like traveling on a dangerous road, sea travel with no news, or disappearance during war or banditry. The Hanafi school is meticulous, requiring that the presumption be grounded in evidence, not mere speculation. The text quotes Jami' al-Fatawa, which extends this further: if the missing person disappears in a Muslim land, the presumption of death is also strong, and the judge may rule accordingly. However, some scholars, including Qadizada, required a long period to elapse. The passage then contrasts this with the Maliki school: Imam Malik allowed the wife to remarry after four years of waiting following the judge's decision, regardless of strong presumption, under certain conditions. Imam Ahmad adopted a similar view. Finally, the passage notes that some later Hanafi scholars (muta'akhkhirin), due to the exigencies of their time, adopted the Maliki opinion by way of legal stratagem (hila) as a dispensation, as reported by Allama Shami quoting Qahistani. The passage ends with a definition of early (mutaqaddimin) and later (muta'akhkhirin) Hanafi scholars: up to the third century are mutaqaddimin, from the fourth century onward are muta'akhkhirin. This lesson is an 'expansion probe' because it expands on the ruling of mafqud with cross-madhhab comparison and historical fatwa development.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A person who has disappeared and whose whereabouts and life/death status are unknown.
غالب گمان (ghalib al-guman): Strong presumption or overwhelming probability, as opposed to mere doubt. It is a basis for legal rulings in the absence of certainty.
متقدمین (mutaqaddimin): Early Hanafi scholars from the first three centuries (up to 300 AH).
متاخرین (muta'akhkhirin): Later Hanafi scholars from the fourth century onwards (after 300 AH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as described in the passage, when may the wife of a missing person remarry?
A) After four years of waiting, regardless of circumstances.
B) Only after the judge rules on the husband's death based on a strong presumption of death, such as disappearance in war or dangerous travel.
C) Immediately upon the husband's disappearance, if she has no children.
D) Only after the husband's contemporaries have all died out, which may take over 90 years.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows, in cases of necessity, adopting the Maliki four-year rule for the wife of a missing person, demonstrating the flexibility of its fatwa hierarchy.

The Mafqud al-Khabar Wife: A Hila via Maliki Fatwa
Sending detailed queries to Maliki scholars to resolve a missing husband case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key issues and procedural steps for resolving the marriage of a mafqud al-khabar's wife through a hila by adopting the Maliki position.

Core Idea
Solving a missing husband case requires a hila from another madhhab because Hanafi law offers no fixed waiting period.

This passage shows how Ashraf Ali Thanwi, faced with a difficult case under Hanafi law (wife of a missing person), turns to Maliki jurists for a practical solution. He sends detailed questions to clarify conditions and procedures. This lesson examines the structure of those questions to understand the issues involved in such a legal stratagem.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
The wife of a mafqud al-khabar (missing person) is in limbo — she cannot remarry because the husband's status is unknown. Under Hanafi law, she must wait indefinitely until death is confirmed.
2
Recognize the need for a hila
Because the Hanafi position offers no convenient solution, the mufti seeks a ruling from the Maliki school, which provides a mechanism for judicial dissolution after a waiting period.
This is a classic example of 'talfiq' (patching) within a single case.
3
Parse the six questions
The questions cover: (1) right to remarry and waiting period, (2) start of the waiting period, (3) wife's autonomy vs. judge's ruling, (4) judge's duty to investigate, (5) procedure in areas without a shar'i judge, (6) applicability in dar al-Islam vs. dar al-harb.
Note the numbering error in the source: questions 1, 3, 3, 4, 5, 6.
4
Note the procedural detail
The correspondence went through three rounds to obtain satisfactory answers, showing the complexity and care required for a hila.
5
Understand the note on 'faskh'
The author clarifies that 'faskh' is used colloquially, not in its technical Hanafi sense, to make the discussion accessible to the common public.
Technical faskh is a specific judicial annulment; here it means any form of dissolution.

Source Text
